<p><b>Elections to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a></b> for the <a href="/wiki/20th_United_States_Congress" title="20th United States Congress">20th Congress</a> were held at various dates in each state in 1826 and 1827.</p>
<p>In these midterm campaigns, the aftershock of the contested <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1824" title="United States presidential election, 1824">1824 presidential election</a> remained a major issue. The former <a href="/wiki/Democratic-Republican_Party" title="Democratic-Republican Party">Democratic-Republican Party</a> had split into two parties, the Jacksonians, supporting <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a> (which would later become the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>) and the Adams men or Anti-Jacksonians, supporters of President <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a>. Adams' supporters would later come to be known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="National Republican Party (United States)">National Republican Party</a>. The Jacksonians were able to pick up a slim majority in the House by painting an image of the Adams Men as elitist and of the Jacksonians as the party of the common farmer or artisan. This tactic helped them pick up a number of rural seats.</p>
<p></p>

<p>Louis McLane (J) resigned before the start of the 20th Congress, having been elected to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senate</a> and was replaced in <a href="/wiki/Delaware%27s_at-large_congressional_district_special_election,_1827" title="Delaware's at-large congressional district special election, 1827">a special election</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kensey_Johns,_Jr." title="Kensey Johns, Jr.">Kensey Johns, Jr.</a> (A)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgia"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Georgia" title="List of United States Representatives from Georgia">Georgia</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1826&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Georgia switched to using districts for this election. Two incumbents, <a href="/wiki/James_Meriwether" title="James Meriwether">James Meriwether</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Cary_(Georgia_politician)" title="George Cary (Georgia politician)">George Cary</a>, did not run for re-election.</p>

Tattnall</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/Georgia%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Georgia's 1st congressional district">1st district</a> resgined in 1827 before the start of the 20th Congress and was replaced in <a href="/wiki/Georgia%27s_1st_congressional_district_special_election,_1827" title="Georgia's 1st congressional district special election, 1827">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/George_Rockingham_Gilmer" title="George Rockingham Gilmer">George R. <p><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Metcalfe_(Kentucky)" title="Thomas Metcalfe (Kentucky)">Thomas Metcalfe</a> (A) of the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Kentucky's 2nd congressional district">2nd district</a> resigned June 1, 1828 to run for <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Kentucky" title="Governor of Kentucky">Governor of Kentucky</a> and was replaced in <a href="/wiki/Kentucky%27s_2nd_congressional_district_special_election,_1828" title="Kentucky's 2nd congressional district special election, 1828">a special election</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Chambers_(Kentucky)" title="John Chambers (Kentucky)">John Chambers</a> (A).</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_S._Young" title="William S. Young">William S. Young</a> (A) of the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky%27s_11th_congressional_district" title="Kentucky's 11th congressional district">11th district</a> died on September 20, 1827. <a href="/wiki/Kentucky%27s_11th_congressional_district_special_elections,_1827" title="Kentucky's 11th congressional district special elections, 1827">Two special elections</a> were subsequently held to fill the resulting vacancy, the first was won by <a href="/wiki/John_Calhoon" title="John Calhoon">John Calhoon</a> (A). Calhoon resigned two days later to avoid an electoral challenge, and a second election was held which was won by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Chilton" title="Thomas Chilton">Thomas Chilton</a> (J)</p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Oakley" title="Thomas J. Oakley">Thomas J. Oakley</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_5th_congressional_district" title="New York's 5th congressional district">5th district</a> resigned May 9, 1828 to become a judge of the superior court of New York City and was replaced in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=New_York%27s_5th_congressional_district_special_election,_1828&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="New York's 5th congressional district special election, 1828 (page does not exist)">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Taber_II" title="Thomas Taber II">Thomas Taber II</a> (J)</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Silas_Wright" title="Silas Wright">Silas Wright</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_20th_congressional_district" title="New York's 20th congressional district">20th district</a> resigned February 16, 1829. His seat remained vacant for the remainder of the 20th Congress (which ended March 3, 1829)</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Ellicott_Evans" title="David Ellicott Evans">David E. Evans</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_29th_congressional_district" title="New York's 29th congressional district">29th district</a> resigned May 27, 1827, before the 20th Congress' first meeting, and was replaced in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=New_York%27s_29th_congressional_district_special_election,_1827&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="New York's 29th congressional district special election, 1827 (page does not exist)">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/Phineas_L._Tracy" title="Phineas L. Tracy">Phineas L. Tracy</a> (A)</p>

<p>Soon after the election, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samuel_P._Carson" title="Samuel P. Carson">Samuel P. Carson</a> (J), the winner of the race in the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina%27s_12th_congressional_district" title="North Carolina's 12th congressional district">12th district</a>, challenged his opponent, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Brank_Vance" title="Robert Brank Vance">Robert B. Vance</a> (A) to a duel over a comment made during the campaign about Carson's father. Vance was mortally wounded in the duel. Carson left immediately afterwards to go to Washington. His behavior in leaving immediately was widely criticized.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<p><a href="/wiki/William_Creighton,_Jr." title="William Creighton, Jr.">William Creighton, Jr.</a> (A) of the <a href="/wiki/Ohio%27s_6th_congressional_district" title="Ohio's 6th congressional district">6th district</a> resigned November 1, 1828 after receiving a <a href="/wiki/Recess_appointment" title="Recess appointment">recess appointment</a> by <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a> to a seat on the Federal bench in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Ohio" title="United States District Court for the District of Ohio">United States District Court for the District of Ohio</a> and was replaced in a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ohio%27s_6th_congressional_district_special_election,_1828&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ohio's 6th congressional district special election, 1828 (page does not exist)">special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/Francis_Swaine_Muhlenberg" title="Francis Swaine Muhlenberg">Francis S. Muhlenberg</a> (A)</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/William_Wilson_(Ohio_politician)" title="William Wilson (Ohio politician)">William Wilson</a> (A) of the <a href="/wiki/Ohio%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Ohio's 8th congressional district">8th district</a> died June 6, 1827, and was replaced in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ohio%27s_8th_congressional_district_special_election,_1827&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ohio's 8th congressional district special election, 1827 (page does not exist)">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/William_Stanbery" title="William Stanbery">William Stanbery</a> (J)</p>

<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Pennsylvania's 2nd congressional district">2nd district</a>, a tie vote occurred, with both Sergent and Horn receiving 1,597 votes. A subsequent <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_2nd_congressional_district_special_election,_1827" title="Pennsylvania's 2nd congressional district special election, 1827">special election</a> was held which elected <a href="/wiki/John_Sergeant_(politician)" title="John Sergeant (politician)">John Sergeant</a>.</p>

<td>1822</td>
<td>Incumbent re-elected.</td>
<td><b>√ <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wharton_Conway" title="Henry Wharton Conway">Henry Conway</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nr_8-10"><a href="#cite_note-nr-8">[Note 8]</a></sup></b></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Florida_Territory%27s_at-large_congressional_district" title="Florida Territory's at-large congressional district">Florida Territory at-large</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Joseph_M._White" title="Joseph M. White">Joseph M. White</a></td>
<td>1824</td>
<td>Incumbent re-elected.</td>
<td><b>√ <a href="/wiki/Joseph_M._White" title="Joseph M. White">Joseph M. White</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nr_8-11"><a href="#cite_note-nr-8">[Note 8]</a></sup></b></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Michigan_Territory%27s_at-large_congressional_district" title="Michigan Territory's at-large congressional district">Michigan Territory at-large</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Austin_Eli_Wing" title="Austin Eli Wing">Austin E. Wing</a></td>
<td>1824</td>
<td>Incumbent re-elected.</td>
<td><b>√ <a href="/wiki/Austin_Eli_Wing" title="Austin Eli Wing">Austin E. Wing</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nr_8-12"><a href="#cite_note-nr-8">[Note 8]</a></sup></b></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Wharton_Conway" title="Henry Wharton Conway">Henry Conway</a> of <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_Territory" title="Arkansas Territory">Arkansas Territory</a> died November 9, 1827 from a duel and was replaced in a special election by <a href="/wiki/Ambrose_Hundley_Sevier" title="Ambrose Hundley Sevier">Ambrose H. Sevier</a></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1826&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Changed from at-large</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Majority required for election, which was not met in the 7th district, requiring additional elections December 18, 1826, April 2, and September 27, 1827</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Includes 1 plural district</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Majority required for election, which was not met on the first vote in 3 districts requiring additional elections held March 5 and May 14, 1827</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Includes 3 plural districts</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Includes 6 plural districts</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Majority required for election, which was not met on the first vote in 2 districts requiring additional elections held December 4, 1826 and February 5, 1827</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-nr-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_8-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Source does not give numbers of votes or has incomplete data</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Unclear whether Tomlinson actually ran or if the votes for him were unsolicited</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-fn-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-fn_10-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn_10-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn_10-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn_10-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn_10-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn_10-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn_10-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Source does not give full name</span></li>
